Commun. 5, 4340 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d14844e2972">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Lam, H. M. et al. Resequencing of 31 wild and cultivated soybean genomes identifies patterns of genetic diversity and selection. Nat. Genet. 42, 1053âU1041 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d14844e2975">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Li, M. W. et al. QTLs regulating the contents of antioxidants, phenolics, and flavonoids in soybean seeds share a common genomic region. Front. Plant Sci. 7, 854 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d14844e2978">14</a></sup>. Information of other soybean accessions used in this study is presented in Supplementary DataÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM10">6</a>.</p><p>For Illumina sequencing, seeds of W05 were germinated on 0.8% water agar in sterile magenta box at 28âÂ°C in dark. Hypocotyls and radicals were collected 3â4 days after germination and snap frozen in liquid nitrogen. DNA was extracted from the hypocotyls and radicals of young W05 seedlings using DNeasy Plant Mini Kit (Qiagen, Hilden, Germany, Cat. 69104). The DNA sample was sent to BGI-Shenzhen (Shenzhen, China) for library construction and sequencing on the Illumina HiSeq2000 platform (Illumina, San Diego, CA).</p><p>For Pacbio sequencing, W05 was grown in greenhouse on regular soil. Trifoliate leaves were collected and snap frozen in liquid nitrogen. Nuclei were isolated from trifoliate leaves of W05 following a published protocol<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Liu, Y. G. &amp; Whittier, R. F. Rapid preparation of megabase plant DNA from nuclei in agarose plugs and microbeads. Nucleic Acids Res. 22, 2168â2169 (1994)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d14844e2991">34</a></sup> with minor modification. Frozen leaves were ground in liquid nitrogen. The powder was suspended in 200âmL nuclei isolation buffer (10âmM Tris HCl pH9.5, 10âmM EDTA, 100âmM KCl, 500âmM sucrose, 4âmM spermidine, 1âmM spermine, and 0.2% (v/v) Î²-mercaptoethanol) with 0.6% (v/v) Triton X-100 and filtered through 41ânm and 20ânm nylon mesh sequentially. The lysate was centrifuged at 1200âÃâ<i>g</i> for 10âmin at 4âÂ°C to collect the nuclei. The nuclei was washed twice with nuclei isolation buffer with Triton X-100 and once with nuclei isolation buffer only. Nuclei DNA was extracted using modified cetyltrimethylammonium bromideÂ (CTAB) method<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Doyle, J. J. A rapid DNA isolation procedure for small quantities of fresh leaf tissue. Phytochem. Bull. Bot. Soc. Am. 19, 11â15 (1987)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d14844e2998">35</a></sup>. The DNA sample was sent to BGI-Shenzhen and Wuhan Institute of Biotechnology (Wuhan, HuBei, China) for library construction and sequencing. In total, 6 SMRTbell libraries with size selection using BluePippin (Sage Science, Beverly, MA) were constructed and sequenced using 72 SMRT cells with P6-C4 chemistry on PacBio RS II platform (Pacific Biosciences, Menlo Park, CA).</p><p>The Dovetail Hi-C library was prepared and sequenced by Dovetail Genomics (Santa Cruz, CA)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Lieberman-Aiden, E. et al. Comprehensive mapping of long-range interactions reveals folding principles of the human genome. Science 326, 289â293 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3005">36</a></sup>. Briefly, chromatin in the nucleus of soybean young seedlings was fixed with formaldehyde and extracted. Fixed chromatin was digested with DpnII and sticky ends were filled in with biotinylated nucleotides and ligated. Crosslinks were then reversed and DNA was purified. Purified DNA was treated to remove biotin that was not internal to ligated fragments. The DNA was then sheared to ~350âbp and sequencing libraries were constructed using NEBNextÂ® Ultraâ¢ DNA Library Prep Kit (Illumina, Cat. E7370S). Biotin-containing fragments were enriched through streptavidin bead pulldown before PCR amplification of the library. The library was sequenced on Illumina HiSeq X platform (Illumina).</p><p>For Bionano OM, young leaves of all the soybean germplasm used in this study were collected from 7- to 10-day-old seedlings grown in greenhouse and high-molecular weight (HMW) DNA was extracted following the Bionano IrysPrepÂ® High Polysaccharides Plant Tissue DNA Isolation User Guide (Bionano Document Number: 30128). Extracted HMW DNA molecules were fluorescently stained using Nick-Label-Repair-Stain (NLRS) enzymatic reactions following the Bionano Prepâ¢ Labeling - NLRS Protocol (Bionano Document Number: 30024). Briefly, single-strand breaks were introduced to DNA molecules by nicking enzyme Nb.BssSI or Nt.BspQI to generate sequence motif-specific patterns. Nicked sites were labeled with fluorescent nucleotides and repaired. Molecule backbones were also fluorescently stained with YOYO-1 to visualize the full lengths.</p><p>NLRS reaction products were then run on Bionano Saphyr (Bionano Genomics, San Diego, CA) for W05 or Irys system (Bionano Genomics) for the rest of the soybean germplasms, where DNA molecules were automatically stretched and imaged within nanochannel arrays. Distances between fluorescently labeled nicking sites form patterns as basis for alignment and assembly by Bionano AutoDetect software (v2.1.4).</p><p>Embryos of W05 were collected 24âh after germination in distilled water, in a dark incubator. Cotyledons and hypocotyl were collected 3 days, whereas root, apical buds, and stems were collected 10 days after sowing in vermiculite with 70% water content and growing in a greenhouse. Flower, 7-day pods, 14-day pods, 14-day seeds, 40-day pods, and 40-day seeds were collected at reproductive stages from soybean plant grown in the greenhouse. Total RNA was extracted using RNAiso Plus reagent (TaKaRa, Kyoto, Japan, Cat. 9108). Nodules and remaining roots were collected 28 days post inoculation with <i>Sinorhizobium fredii</i> strain CCBAU45436<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Tian, C. F. et al. Comparative genomics of rhizobia nodulating soybean suggests extensive recruitment of lineage-specific genes in adaptations. Proc. Natl Acad. Sci. USA 109, 8629â8634 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3022">37</a></sup>. Total RNA was extracted from nodules and the remaining roots were extracted using TRIzolÂ® reagent (Thermo Fisher Scientific, Waltham, MA, Cat. 15596018).</p><p>RNA samples were sent out to BGI-Shenzhen for both RNA sequencing (RNA-seq) and PacBio IsoSeq. For RNA-seq, stranded RNA-seq libraries were constructed for each RNA sample and sequenced on Illumina HiSeq4000 platform (Illumina). For PacBio IsoSeq, equal amount of RNA from different tissues were pooled. Four SMRTbell libraries were constructed with size selection of 1â2âKb, 2â3âKb, 3â6âKb, and 5â10âKb using the BluePippin (Sage Science), and sequenced with 4, 4, 2, 2 SMRT cells with P6-C4 chemistry on PacBio RS II platform (Pacific Biosciences).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12">
                           <b>De novo</b> genome assembly</h3><p>Before de novo assembly, low-quality PacBio subreads with a read length shorter than 500âbp or a quality score lower than 0.8 were filtered out. The remaining clean PacBio subreads were error-corrected and assembled into contigs with MECAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Xiao, C. L. et al. MECAT : fast mapping, error correction, and de novo assembly for single-molecule sequencing reads. Nat. Methods 14, 1072â1074 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3041">38</a></sup> (version 1.0). The MECAT de novo assembler is composed of three major steps: (i) mecat2pw: all vs. all alignment between PacBio subreads were performed; (ii) mecat2cns: high-quality consensus reads were generated with parameter setting: -a 2000 -c 4 -l 2000; and (iii) mecat2canu: 40âÃ longest high-quality consensus reads were assembled into primary contigs with parameter setting: genomeSizeâ=â1100000000 ErrorRateâ=â0.013.</p><p>All clean PacBio subreads were mapped to the assembled contigs using pbalign (SMRTLink package release 4.0.0.190159). The primary contigs were polished with mapped PacBio subreads using Quiver implementation in variantCaller (SMRTLink package release 4.0.0.190159).</p><p>Illumina short reads with insert size of 250, 500, and 800âbp were used to correct residual errors in the polished contigs. Reads contain adapter sequences or 5% Ns, or with low quality, or derived from PCR artifacts were filtered.</p><p>Remaining clean reads were mapped to polished contigs using Burrows-Wheeler Aligner (BWA) mem<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Li H. Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. Preprint at https://arxivorg/abs/13033997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3054">39</a></sup> (version 0.7.15-r1142) with default parameters. Duplicated reads were tagged using Picard MarkDuplicates implementation (<a href="https://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/">https://broadinstitute.github.io/picard/</a>, version 2.9.0â1-gf5b9f50), with default parameters. Residual errors in the polished contigs were corrected with mapped next generation sequencing (NGS) reads using Pilon<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Walker, B. J. et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS ONE 9, e112963 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3065">40</a></sup> (version 1.22), with the following parameter setting: âdiploidâfix snps,indels,local. Polished contigs were used as input for scaffolding analysis.</p><p>For scaffolding, HiRise<sup>TM</sup> pipeline (Dovetail Genomics) was used for scaffolding<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Putnam, N. H. et al. Chromosome-scale shotgun assembly using an in vitro method for long-range linkage. Genome Res. 26, 342â350 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3075">41</a></sup>. Hi-C reads and NGS clean reads with insert size of 250, 500, and 800âbp were mapped to polished contigs using modified Scalable Nucleotide Alignment Program (SNAP) mapper (<a href="http://snap.cs.berkeley.edu">http://snap.cs.berkeley.edu</a>). Repeats in the contigs were masked, based on NGS read mapping depth. The order and orientation of contigs within Hi-C scaffolds were determined based on contact frequency calculated from mapped Hi-C read pairs.</p><p>Low-quality optical molecules with molecule lengthâ&lt;â150âKb or molecule signal intensityâ&gt;â0.6, or molecule label numberâ&lt;â9 were removed. Optical molecules digested with Nt.BspQI or Nb.BssSI were de novo assembled into optical contigs using Bionano Solve<sup>TM</sup> (v3.0.1 release v06082017, parameter settings: Iteration:5; minlen:150âkb; minsites:9; initialAssembly: 1.00Eâââ10; extendRefine: 1.00Eâââ11; merge: 1.00Eâââ15). Two-enzyme hybrid scaffolding were performed using Bionano Solve<sup>TM</sup> (v3.0.1 release v06082017, default parameters) with polished contig sequences and two set of de novo assembled optical contigs as input to generate hybrid scaffolds.</p><p>Superscaffolds were generated by merging Hi-C scaffolds and hybrid scaffolds. Linkages between adjacent contigs within superscaffolds were classified into three categories based on supporting evidence: (i) both: linkage supported by both Hi-C scaffolds and hybrid scaffolds; (ii) map: linkage supported only by hybrid scaffolds; and (iii) Hi-C: linkage supported only by Hi-C scaffolds.</p><p>To fill and close gaps, PacBio subreads were mapped to superscaffolds using BLASR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Chaisson, M. J. &amp; Tesler, G. Mapping single molecule sequencing reads using basic local alignment with successive refinement (BLASR): application and theory. BMC Bioinformatics 13, 238 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3099">42</a></sup> (version 1.3.1.142244). Gaps within the superscaffolds were filled with consensus sequences generated from PacBio subreads that span or flank gaps using PBJelly2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="English, A. C. et al. Mind the gap: upgrading genomes with Pacific Biosciences RS Long-Read Sequencing Technology. PLoS ONE 7, e47768 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3103">43</a></sup> (PBSuite_15.8.24). After gap filling, another round of polishing was performed with PacBio subreads and Illumina short reads to eliminate sequence errors in the filled sequences.</p><p>Gaps within the superscaffolds were closed by searching for gap-flanking sequences that were identical to each other in a head-to-tail way using BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3110">44</a></sup> (version 2.2.31, default parameter). Illumina mate-pair reads with insert size of 2, 6, and 10âKb, and optical molecules were used to distinguish redundant sequences from true tandem repeated sequences. Illumina mate-pair reads with different insert sizes were mapped to superscaffolds with BWA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows-Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3114">45</a></sup> aln implementation (version 0.7.15-r1142, parameter settings: -a 50000). Optical molecules were aligned to the in silico digested map of superscaffolds with OMBlast<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Leung, A. K. Y. et al. OMBlast: alignment tool for optical mapping using a seed-and-extend approach. Bioinformatics 33, 311â319 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3118">46</a></sup> (version 1.4a) and visualized with OMTools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Leung, A. K. Y., Jin, N., Yip, K. Y. &amp; Chan, T. F. OMTools: a software package for visualizing and processing optical mapping data. Bioinformatics 33, 2933â2935 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3122">47</a></sup> (version 1.4a). For gaps with identical flanking sequences, insert size for mate-pair reads and signal pattern for optical molecules that span or flank these gaps were manually inspected, to identify redundant sequences that were then trimmed to close the gaps. Another round of sequence polishing was performed, with Illumina short reads to eliminate residual errors.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Assembly evaluation</h3><p>The gene completeness of soybean assemblies was evaluated at the contig level using both the PacBio IsoSeq full-length reads and the 1440 conserved BUSCOs. PacBio IsoSeq full-length reads were mapped to genome assemblies using BLAT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Kent, W. J. BLAT - the BLAST-like alignment tool. Genome Res. 12, 656â664 (2002)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3134">48</a></sup> (version 35) with default parameters. Only one best hit was retained for each query sequence. The BLAT alignment hits were further filtered based on mapping identity (ââ¥95%) and query coverage (â¥50% or â¥90%). BUSCO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Simao, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3138">16</a></sup> (version 3.0.2, lineage dataset embryophyta_odb9) was used to identify conserved BUSCO genes in the genome assemblies. Telomeric repeats were identified by tandem repeat finder (TRF)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573â580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3142">49</a></sup> (version 4.0.4). Centromeric repeats were identified by BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3146">44</a></sup> (version 2.2.31, <i>E</i>-valueâ&lt;â1eâââ5) search Cent91/92 sequences against the genome sequence<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Gill, N. et al. Molecular and chromosomal evidence for allopolyploidy in soybean. Plant Physiol. 151, 1167â1174 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3154">17</a></sup>. Primer sequences of soybean genetic map were downloaded from SoyBase (<a href="https://www.soybase.org/dlpages/#geneticmap">https://www.soybase.org/dlpages/#geneticmap</a>). In silico PCR was performed using isPCR (<a href="https://github.com/bowhan/kent/tree/master/src/isPcr/isPcr">https://github.com/bowhan/kent/tree/master/src/isPcr/isPcr</a>), e-PCR<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Rotmistrovsky, K., Jang, W. &amp; Schuler, G. D. A web server for performing electronic PCR. Nucleic Acids Res. 32, W108âW112 (2004)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3172">50</a></sup> (version 2.3.9, parameters: Dâ=â30â1000âNâ=â2âGâ=â2âTâ=â4), and BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3176">44</a></sup> (version 2.2.31, <i>E</i>-valueâ&lt;â1eâââ5). Only primer pairs that mapped to the genome with proper orientation (forward-reverse or reverse-forward) and proper insert size (&lt;â1000âbp) were retained. Primer pairs that have multiple best hits in the genome were filtered.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Repeat annotation</h3><p>Tandem repeats in the genome assembly was identified using TRF<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573â580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3191">49</a></sup> (version 4.0.4). Well-characterized TEs were identified by searching against W05 genome assembly at DNA level and protein level using RepeatMasker (version 4.0.7) (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>) and ProteinRepeatMask (version 4.0.7) (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>) with RepBase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Bao, W. D., Kojima, K. K. &amp; Kohany, O. Repbase update, a database of repetitive elements in eukaryotic genomes. Mob. DNA 6, 11 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3209">51</a></sup> (release 20.04) as the query library. To identify TEs that were absent in the RepBase library, a de novo repeat library was constructed using Repeatmodeler (version 1.0.10) (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>). RepeatMasker was run against the genome assembly again, with de novo repeat library as the query library.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Gene annotation</h3><p>For homology-based evidence generation, the sequences of proteins from <i>Arabidopsis thaliana</i> (araport11), <i>Lotus japonicas</i> (3.0, ftp://ftp.kazusa.or.jp/pub/lotus/lotus_r3.0/), <i>G. max</i> (Phytozome release 12), <i>Vitis vinifera</i> (Phytozome release 12), <i>Medicago truncatula</i> (Phytozome release 12), <i>Prunus persica</i> (Phytozome release 12), and <i>Populus trichocarpa</i> (Phytozome release 12) were downloaded. For each species, only the longest protein sequences were retained as the representative for each gene locus. The representative protein sequences were mapped to <i>G. soja</i> W05 genome using splice-site-aware aligner Exonerate<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Slater, G. S. &amp; Birney, E. Automated generation of heuristics for biological sequence comparison. BMC Bioinformatics 6, 31 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3254">52</a></sup> (version 2.4.0) with the following parameters: âmodel protein2genomeâshowalignmentâshowtargetgffârefine region. Only the best alignment with the highest score was retained for each mapped gene locus for each species.</p><p>For expression-based evidence generation, low-quality RNA-seq reads were filtered and trimmed using trim_galore (version 0.4.1) (<a href="http://www.bioinformatics.babraham.ac.uk/projects/trim_galore/">http://www.bioinformatics.babraham.ac.uk/projects/trim_galore/</a>). Trimmed reads with read length shorter than 80âbp were discarded. Stranded and non-stranded RNA-seq reads were assembled into stranded and non-stranded unigenes using Trinity<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Full-length transcriptome assembly from RNA-Seq data without a reference genome. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644âU130 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3268">53</a></sup> (version 2.4.0) with default parameters, respectively. The assembled stranded and non-stranded unigenes were mapped to genome sequences and assembled into non-redundant transcripts using PASApipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 5654â5666 (2003)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3272">54</a></sup> (version 2.2.0) with the following parameter setting: âMAX_INTRON_LENGTH 20000. Furthermore, consensus PacBio IsoSeq subreads were extracted, classified, and clustered to generate corrected consensus reads using SMRTanalysis package (smrtanalysis_2.3.0.140936). Corrected consensus sequences with low-quality score were further corrected with stranded RNA-seq reads using proovread<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Hackl, T., Hedrich, R., Schultz, J. &amp; Forster, F. proovread: large-scale high-accuracy PacBio correction through iterative short read consensus. Bioinformatics 30, 3004â3011 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3276">55</a></sup> (version 2.13.12, parameter setting: âmode sr). After correction, the consensus sequences were mapped to the genome assembly and assembled into non-redundant transcripts using PASApipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 5654â5666 (2003)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3280">54</a></sup> (version 2.2.0) with parameters: âMAX_INTRON_LENGTH 20000.</p><p>For evidence synthesis and alternative spliced isoform annotation, transcripts that were well supported by both homology-based evidence and expression-based evidence were selected for parameter training for ab initio prediction software Augustus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Stanke, M., Diekhans, M., Baertsch, R. &amp; Haussler, D. Using native and syntenically mapped cDNA alignments to improve de novo gene finding. Bioinformatics 24, 637â644 (2008)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3287">56</a></sup> (version 3.2.3). All the generated transcript evidences mentioned above and trained Augustus parameters were fed into Maker<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Campbell, M. S., Holt, C., Moore, B. &amp; Yandell, M. Genome annotation and curation using MAKER and MAKER-P. Curr. Protoc. Bioinformatics 48, 4.11.11â14.11.39 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3291">57</a></sup> (version 2.31.9) for evidence synthesis to generate primary protein-coding gene set. The primary gene set and expression-data-based evidence were fed into PASApipeline<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Improving the Arabidopsis genome annotation using maximal transcript alignment assemblies. Nucleic Acids Res. 31, 5654â5666 (2003)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3295">54</a></sup> (version 2.2.0) for gene structure refinement and alternative spliced isoform annotation.</p><p>Potential function was assigned to each annotated protein sequence using InterProScan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236â1240 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3302">58</a></sup> (version 5.29â68.0) by searching all available databases with corresponding utilities. Completeness of the annotated gene set was evaluated by BUSCO<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Simao, F. A., Waterhouse, R. M., Ioannidis, P., Kriventseva, E. V. &amp; Zdobnov, E. M. BUSCO: assessing genome assembly and annotation completeness with single-copy orthologs. Bioinformatics 31, 3210â3212 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3306">16</a></sup> (version 3.0.2, lineage dataset embryophyta_odb9).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">ncRNA annotation</h3><p>rRNA sequences of <i>G. max</i> were downloaded from NCBI GenBank database (GenBank ID: X15199.1, AJ009787.1, X02623.1, and AH001766.2). These rRNA sequences were mapped to <i>G. soja</i> W05 genome assembly using BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinformatics 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3324">44</a></sup> (version 2.2.31) with default parameters.</p><p>tRNAScan-SE<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955â964 (1997)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3331">59</a></sup> (version 1.3.1) was used to search the <i>G. soja</i> W05 genome assembly for tRNAs genes with default parameters. Annotated tRNA genes that were classified as Pseudo were filtered.</p><p>To identify miRNA and snRNA genes, infernal<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics 29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3341">60</a></sup> (version 1.1.2, parameters: âcut_gaârfamânohmmonly) was used to search the <i>G. soja</i> W05 genome assembly based on covariance models deposited in Rfam<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Kalvari, I. et al. Rfam 13.0: shifting to a genome-centric resource for non-coding RNA families. Nucleic Acids Res. 46, D335âD342 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3348">61</a></sup> database (release 13.0).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Binmap construction and QTL identification</h3><p>Binmap construction and QTL identification was performed with population sequencing and phenotype datasets generated in our previous studies<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Qi, X. P. et al. Identification of a novel salt tolerance gene in wild soybean by whole-genome sequencing. Nat. Commun. 5, 4340 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3360">8</a></sup> using a slightly modified analysis pipeline. Briefly, short reads from the 96 RI lines were mapped to the genome sequence using BWA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Li, H. &amp; Durbin, R. Fast and accurate short read alignment with Burrows-Wheeler transform. Bioinformatics 25, 1754â1760 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3364">45</a></sup> (version 0.7.15-r1140) with default parameters. Properly and uniquely mapped reads were extracted to identify SNPs using Samtools<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078â2079 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3368">62</a></sup> (version 1.2) with parameter setting: SNP quality valueâ&gt;â30 and &lt;â3 SNPs were allowed in any 10âbp window. Heterozygous or non- parental line-derived SNPs were filtered. At least 20 RI lines were required to have SNPs at each SNP locus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Qi, X. P. et al. Identification of a novel salt tolerance gene in wild soybean by whole-genome sequencing. Nat. Commun. 5, 4340 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3372">8</a></sup>. Recombination breakpoints were identified using a modified sliding window approach (window size: 15 SNPs, step size: 1 SNP)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Huang, X. H. et al. High-throughput genotyping by whole-genome resequencing. Genome Res. 19, 1068â1076 (2009)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3376">63</a></sup>. Adjacent 50âKb intervals were merged into bins if no recombination events were identified from sequenced RI lines. Genetic distance among bins was calculated using R/qtl package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Broman, K. W., Wu, H., Sen, S. &amp; Churchill, G. A. R/qtl: QTL mapping in experimental crosses. Bioinformatics 19, 889â890 (2003)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3381">64</a></sup> (version 1.41.6, default parameters). QTLs for each agronomical trait were identified using QTL Cartographer (<a href="http://statgen.ncsu.edu/qtlcart/">http://statgen.ncsu.edu/qtlcart/</a>) (version 1.17j) with a 10âcM scanning window and a 0.5âcM step size. For each agronomical trait, logarithm of the odds (LOD) cutoff was determined by 1000 permutation of the phenotypes and genotypes with significance level of <i>Î±</i>â&lt;â0.05 using QTL Cartographer. Peaks having LOD value higher than the LOD cutoff were considered as significant. For green seed phenotype dataset, only RI lines of the green and yellow seeds were used. For seed size phenotype dataset, about 35 seeds from each RI line were measured using SmartGrain<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Tanabata, T., Shibaya, T., Hori, K., Ebana, K. &amp; Yano, M. SmartGrain: high-throughput phenotyping software for measuring seed shape through image analysis. Plant Physiol. 160, 1871â1880 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3395">65</a></sup> (version 1.1).</p><p>For the same QTL for each agronomical trait, sequence alignment was performed between two QTL regions (with referenced to different genomes) using the nucmer program from MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Marcais, G. et al. MUMmer4: a fast and versatile genome alignment system. PLoS Comput. Biol. 14, e1005944 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3402">66</a></sup> (version 4.0), with default parameter. Aligned block with length smaller than 1âKb were filtered. The overall aligned region was defined as overlapped region.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Genome-wide TE insertion identification</h3><p>Repeat elements in cultivated soybean genomes were annotated using the same pipeline as used for W05 genome repeat annotation. To identify TE insertions in Wm82_v2 and ZH13 genomes, the two genomes were aligned to W05. In reverse, the W05 genome was compared with those of Wm82 and ZH13 for W05-specific insertions. Genome comparisons were performed using nucmer from MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Marcais, G. et al. MUMmer4: a fast and versatile genome alignment system. PLoS Comput. Biol. 14, e1005944 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3414">66</a></sup> (version 4.0) with parameters: âmumânoextend. Adjacent alignment blocks with a gap lengthâ&gt;â1000âbp in query genome andâ&lt;100âbp in reference genome were identified as insertions in the query genome. If &gt;80% of the inserted regions in the query genome were annotated as TE elements, the insertion was defined as a TE insertion and the corresponding alignment gap in the reference genome was defined as a TE insertion site. If a TE insertion site in the reference genome was located within a genic region or a 500âbp flanking genic region, then genes were defined as TE-affected genes in the query genome. GO enrichment analysis was performed for TE-affected genes using BINGO (version 3.0.3)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Maere, S., Heymans, K. &amp; Kuiper, M. BiNGO: a Cytoscape plugin to assess overrepresentation of Gene Ontology categories in Biological Networks. Bioinformatics 21, 3448â3449 (2005)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3418">67</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec19">Whole-genome sequence comparison</h3><p>Whole-genome comparison between wild soybean W05 and two cultivated soybean genomes were performed using nucmer from MUMmer package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Marcais, G. et al. MUMmer4: a fast and versatile genome alignment system. PLoS Comput. Biol. 14, e1005944 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3430">66</a></sup> (version 4.0) and visualized with mummerplot from MUMmer package (version 4.0). Large structural variations (&gt;100âKb) were identified based on synteny alignment blocks, with variation boundaries manually checked.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec20">Optical map analysis of multiple soybean accessions</h3><p>To enhance result quality, quality assessment using DataQualityCheck module<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Leung, A. K. Y., Jin, N., Yip, K. Y. &amp; Chan, T. F. OMTools: a software package for visualizing and processing optical mapping data. Bioinformatics 33, 2933â2935 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3442">47</a></sup> was performed to exclude optical molecules from scans with possible anomalies. Throughput, signal-to-noise ratios and alignment rates in datasets were indentified using a reference in silico map. They were checked for deviations from the norm, which may indicate clogging of the nanochannel arrays.</p><p>OM de novo assembly was performed as follows. Filtered optical molecules were assembled into optical contigs using Bionano Solve (version 3.1) assembly pipeline (pipelineCL.py), with parameters optimized by Bionano (optArguments_nonhaplotype_irys.xml; -minlen 150, -minsites 9; merge: 1.00Eâââ15), with <i>p</i>-value cutoff thresholds for initialAssembly and extendRefine modified according to genome size to 1Eâââ8 and 1Eâââ9, respectively.</p><p>For better accuracy in downstream analysis, assembled optical contigs were preprocessed with the OMTools DataTools module before alignment. In consideration of the resolution of signal detection, signals within 1âKb apart were merged for both optical molecules and optical contigs to improve alignment accuracy at regions of dense signals. Optical contigs containing only repetitive segments were removed by OMTools (version 1.4a) DataTools module with the lowden parameter. Processed optical molecules were aligned to retained optical contigs with OMblast (version 1.4a)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Leung, A. K. Y. et al. OMBlast: alignment tool for optical mapping using a seed-and-extend approach. Bioinformatics 33, 311â319 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3455">46</a></sup>. Optical contigs with optical molecule coverage lower than 30 at the target region were excluded from subsequent comparative analysis.</p><p>To locate the coordinates of the optical contigs, sequence assemblies of W05, Wm82, and ZH13 were in silico digested for alignment. Signals on the in silico maps within 1âKb were merged. For each region of interest, optical contigs or in silico maps were aligned to the W05 reference in silico map with OMBlast<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Leung, A. K. Y. et al. OMBlast: alignment tool for optical mapping using a seed-and-extend approach. Bioinformatics 33, 311â319 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3462">46</a></sup>. Pairwise alignment was performed between optical contigs that aligned to the target region. Multiple alignment of the optical contigs was then performed to obtain linkage information of genome segments using Optical Map Multiple Alignment package (<a href="https://github.com/TF-Chan-Lab/OMTools">https://github.com/TF-Chan-Lab/OMTools</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Leung, A. K. Y., Jin, N., Yip, K. Y. &amp; Chan, T. F. OMTools: a software package for visualizing and processing optical mapping data. Bioinformatics 33, 2933â2935 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3473">47</a></sup> (version 1.4a). Signal patterns and linkage information were compared, to characterize genomic structural variations among germplasms.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">PCR verification of the inversion junction at the <i>I</i> locus</h3><p>To verify the inversion in the <i>I</i> locus of soybeans with colorless seed coat, junction of the inversion that created the subtilisin-anti-<i>CHS1</i> chimeric transcript were amplified from genomic DNA of selected soybean accessions. For the detection of subtilisin-anti-<i>CHS1</i> chimeric transcript, RNA was extracted from the seed coat of developing seeds of Wm82 and W05 using Fruit-mate<sup>TM</sup> for RNA purification (Takara, Cat. 9192) and RNAiso Plus reagent (Takara, Cat. 9108). First-strand cDNAs and subsequent PCR were done using One-Step TB Greenâ¢ PrimeScriptâ¢ RT-PCR Kit II (Takara, Cat. RR086). In the reverse-transcription step, only the reverse primer specific for either the subtilisin-anti-<i>CHS1</i> chimeric transcript or the <i>GmACT11</i> gene<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Guimaraes-Dias, F. et al. Expression analysis in response to drought stress in soybean: shedding light on the regulation of metabolic pathway genes. Genet. Mol. Biol. 35, 222âU259 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3508">68</a></sup> (housekeeping gene) was added. Forward primers were then added for the subsequent PCR amplification. Primer information can be found in Supplementary TableÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM1">12</a>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Hi-C contact frequency calculation</h3><p>Hi-C raw reads were mapped to W05 genome and Hi-C contact frequency between genomic loci was computed using Juicer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicer provides a one-click system for analyzing loop-resolution Hi-C experiments. Cell Syst. 3, 95â98 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3523">69</a></sup> (version 1.5) with window size of 100âKb. The Hi-C reads contact frequency matrix was visualized using Juicebox<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Durand, N. C. et al. Juicebox provides a visualization system for Hi-C contact maps with unlimited zoom. Cell Syst. 3, 99â101 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d14844e3527">70</a></sup> (version 1.5.2).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Reporting summary</h3><p>Further information on experimental design is available in theÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM3">Nature Research Reporting Summary</a> linked to this article.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>Genome assembly and annotations data of <i>G. soja</i> W05 were deposited in the DDBJ/ENA/GenBank under accession QZWG00000000 [<a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/assembly/GCA_004193775.1/">https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/assembly/GCA_004193775.1/</a>]. The version described here is version QZWG01000000. All the raw sequencing reads were deposited in the NCBI Sequence Read Archive database under the accession <a href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/sra/?term=SRP158454">SRP158454</a>. The optical molecules and optical contigs of W05 were deposited as NCBIÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM1">Supplementary Files</a> under accession SUPPF_0000002760 [ftp://ftp.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pub/supplementary_data/bionanomaps.csv] and SUPPF_0000002761 [ftp://ftp.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pub/supplementary_data/bionanomaps.csv]. The optical contigs of other soybean accessions were deposited as NCBI Supplementary Files under accessions SUPPF_0000002797-SUPPF_0000002807 [ftp://ftp.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pub/supplementary_data/bionanomaps.csv]. W05 genome assembly and annotation are also available at wildsoydb database (<a href="http://www.wildsoydb.org/Gsoja_W05">www.wildsoydb.org/Gsoja_W05</a>). Seeds of the sequenced wild soybean accession W05 cannot be freely distributed to scientists outside of China due to legal restrictions on the exchange of wild plant germplasms. However, seeds of the other parental line C08 and the derived recombinant inbreeding lines are available from Hon-Ming Lam (honming@cuhk.edu.hk) upon request. Data supporting the findings of this work are available within the paper and itsÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM1">Supplementary Information files</a>. A reporting summary for this article is available as aÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM1">Supplementary Information file</a>. The datasets generated and analyzed during the current study are available from the corresponding author on reasonable request. The source data for Fig.Â <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM11">2b</a> and Supplementary FigureÂ <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-019-09142-9#MOESM1">6</a> are provided as a Source Data file.</p>

                <ul data-test="author-list"
                    class="c-article-further-reading__authors-list js-list-authors-3 js-etal-collapsed" data-component-authors-activator="authors-list"
                    id="authors-3">
                  <li><span
                        class="js-separator"></span><span>Jong Hum Kim</span></li><li><span

              <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-3">
                <i>Current Opinion in Plant Biology</i>
                (2021)
              </p>
            </li>
